<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_99b1a8c3-c0e8-40ef-bda4-7ce39a3508af'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText9038724947593684661" style="display:none"><b>A love letter to the craft and romance of film and fate in front of—and behind—the camera from the award-winning author of <i>Hold Still.</i></b><br />  <br /> A wunderkind young set designer, Emi has already started to find her way in the competitive Hollywood film world.<br />  <br /> Emi is a film buff and a true romantic, but her real-life relationships are a mess. She has desperately gone back to the same girl too many times to mention. But then a mysterious letter from a silver screen legend leads Emi to Ava. Ava is unlike anyone Emi has ever met. She has a tumultuous, not-so-glamorous past, and lives an unconventional life. She’s enigmatic…. She’s beautiful. And she is about to expand Emi’s understanding of family, acceptance, and true romance.<br />  </span>

<div id="review_3039650800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3039650800" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3039650800?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=sapphic">sapphic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3039650800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10129788602960644471">I'm trying to get back into audiobooks, and knowing that contemporary and memoirs are the funnest to listen to, I gave this one a try. I really enjoyed the narrator and the story, so it was a fun listen! But I proved to myself that once again, I have a tendency to let details slip through the cracks when I listen to audiobooks.<br/><br/>The main thing I enjoyed about this book is the characters. I thought Emi was a good lens from which the story is told, and her friendships with Charlotte and Ava were so </span>
  <span id="freeText10129788602960644471" style="display:none">I'm trying to get back into audiobooks, and knowing that contemporary and memoirs are the funnest to listen to, I gave this one a try. I really enjoyed the narrator and the story, so it was a fun listen! But I proved to myself that once again, I have a tendency to let details slip through the cracks when I listen to audiobooks.<br /><br />The main thing I enjoyed about this book is the characters. I thought Emi was a good lens from which the story is told, and her friendships with Charlotte and Ava were so cute and realistic. I rarely read books that are just strictly fun anymore, so this was a lovely change of pace that kept me interested even though I'm not the biggest fan of books about the movie industry. Ava and Emi had great chemistry, and I like that this book talked about the difference between movies and real life, how people glamorize one another, and how in reality, real life is so different than in movies. <br /><br />I know this shouldn't be an official part of my review, but I just can't help but mention that it warms my heart to see books with f/f relationships where the entire plot of the book isn't about 1) everyone around that character being homophobic, or 2) the two characters spending the entire book not knowing if the other is straight. This book cuts straight to normalizing same sex relationships and talking about it openly, so they chemistry and angst that occurs all stems from the plot occurring, not internally, which I find so much more interesting and less repetitive. In the end, I loved the relationship that occurred in this book and how the build up to it was so subtle and supportive.<br /><br />For a fun contemporary featuring a lesbian relationship, I got everything I wanted from it. Even though it's not a full five stars to me, it still was highly enjoyable and didn't really even have any major flaws. I'm kind of just pulling comments out of my ass to finish this review because audiobooks are difficult to review since I forget the content so quickly after I read them. But anyway, read this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1585931044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1585931044" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1585931044?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sapphic-books-shelf">sapphic-books-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1585931044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15711985816441300337"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“We love films because they makes us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into the eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing. But also. They tell us to remember; they remind us of life. Remember, they say, how much it hurts to have your heart broken.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Everything Leads to You</i> is a book about movies and lesbian love, and even though it didn’t impress me as much as I’d hoped, it's a</span>
  <span id="freeText15711985816441300337" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“We love films because they makes us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into the eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing. But also. They tell us to remember; they remind us of life. Remember, they say, how much it hurts to have your heart broken.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>Everything Leads to You</i> is a book about movies and lesbian love, and even though it didn’t impress me as much as I’d hoped, it's a really incredible story and definitely worth the hype. <br /><br />The main character, Emi, is an aspiring film worker. I loved the descriptions and depictions of her sets. I’m not a movie person, but if I were, this would’ve been amazing. Anyone who loves movies will absolutely LOVE this book, but honestly, even without loving cinema, LaCour’s writing was <b>visual</b> enough that I could picture everything. <br /><br />Emi’s arc is about realizing she can’t idealize people, and that she can’t idealize the happy endings of movies either. It’s a <b>well-executed arc</b>; it ties in nicely with her new career and with her new relationship. <br /><br />There's a romance here between Emi and a girl she's just met, Ava. Ava is a likable character with a bit of mystery surrounding her past, and also, I'm realizing writing this that she shares a name with a girl I have a crush on! Tea. Unfortunately, I thought the romance here overtook things just a bit, which would've been fine if the romance were spectacular, but frankly, <b>the romance was good, not great.</b> Neither this particular romance nor the movie-star plotline were quite good enough to hold this up for me, which again, is primarily a personal problem. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“They weren't cheap and I was almost broke. It was a choice between dinner and flowers and I chose flowers because it was a dark time in my life and my room was hideous and my heart was broken and I needed something beautiful.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I honestly don’t have many complaints about this book, but I somehow didn’t enjoy it, in my 2016 reading, as much as I probably should have. I liked it, but I didn’t obsess over it. That being said, I think this was a complete case of “it’s not me, it’s you” and I do want to recommend this to anyone who wants more books about gay girls and about the movies. I also think this is one I should probably reread soon, as I was incredibly uninterested in both film and romance at age fifteen and now... am a huge cinephile who is aggressively in love with love and would like to read 30000 books about girls kissing. <br /><br />TW: abusive / toxic parenting, overdose death. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15711985816441300337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_995681501" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/995681501" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/995681501?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101593509" href="/book/show/18207188-everything-leads-to-you">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      Goodreads--and we love it.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=celebrity">celebrity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer995681501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer373912564739014130">Also posted on <a href='http://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hit or Miss Books</a>.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18667779.Everything_Leads_to_You' title='Everything Leads to You by Nina LaCour' rel='nofollow noopener'>Everything Leads to You</a> is definitely not a BAD book. It was actually my first lesbian YA (romance—details later) read and I think I may continue with this genre and try to seek some gems out there—because there always are! <br/><br/>The story revolves around Ava, the granddaughter of a well-known celebrity who died and left her a letter telling her how much he wished he knew her and that he left her A LOT of money she can use at her sake. Now here is the thing: I thought </span>
  <span id="freeText373912564739014130" style="display:none">Also posted on <a href="http://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hit or Miss Books</a>.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18667779.Everything_Leads_to_You" title="Everything Leads to You by Nina LaCour" rel="nofollow noopener">Everything Leads to You</a> is definitely not a BAD book. It was actually my first lesbian YA (romance—details later) read and I think I may continue with this genre and try to seek some gems out there—because there always are! <br /><br />The story revolves around Ava, the granddaughter of a well-known celebrity who died and left her a letter telling her how much he wished he knew her and that he left her A LOT of money she can use at her sake. Now here is the thing: I thought Emi was the main character. She’s the narrator and there’s a first person POV so it makes it even more obvious. But, even if Emi was the one discovering the letter, everything else important happening revolves, as I said, around Ava. Eveything Leads to Ava. Emi has a new job and then Ava has one as well for the same people. Emi help her find the truth about her mother who died unfortunately too. Ava is struggling with finding a place where she can feel at home and Emi helps her. So, I guess there are really TWO main characters with the same importance level in this book that are connected to each other. The fact is that I was confused about who IS the main main character throughout the story. I guess I'm just not used to LaCour's formula. <br /><br />I thought the ‘mystery’ was completely predictable. I wanted to tell myself it isn’t and struggled to not predict things that were happening but it was too hard not to since it was so simple to deduct. Sometimes predictable stories are not boring, especially contemporary ones and this is one of them. Now I’m not saying that I really enjoyed it still because there are other factors that made me not enjoy this book that much.<br /><br />IT’S FILLED WITH DIALOGS. The many dialogs and few descriptions of places and the world around them annoyed my reading experience. Sometimes dialogs were half page long and that made me take a lot of breaks from this book. I usually read a book in 1-2 days but this one took me 3 days.<br /><br />Emi and Ava are both nice girls and characters. The ‘coincidence’ of them both being lesbian made this book unfortunately not so realistic. I mean, I believe in fate and destiny from time to time but this is too much. If she were bi, then maybe this book would’ve been more realistic. <br /><br />Another problem I had with this book is that there barely is romance! There is only one single kiss in the story and RARE flirting. Of course, there is some mention of girls from Emi’s past and Ava’s as well but nothing substantial. <br /><br />What I liked though was the film part of this book. Really enjoyed knowing more about how it works in that industry and how designers have an immense part in the conception. Emi’s job is one hell of a cool one. Plus, she’s really talented.<br /><br />Overall, I think, if you wish to read a book in which there is mention of the celebrities’ world and film/series as well, I’d recommend The Secrets of My Hollywood Life (LOVED IT) series by Jen Calonita. Also, if you really want romance, I have no recommendations since it’s my first lesbian book but I don’t think this is the one for you. Again, not BAD but not worth of your time if your TBR pile is huge.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="373912564739014130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2780649604?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" class="user" itemprop="url" name="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" href="/user/show/52488949-lia">˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52488949-lia?shelf=2019-favorites">2019-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52488949-lia?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52488949-lia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2780649604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8281590853452854107"><i> “as much as i had wanted a love story out of a movie, i know now that movies can only hope to capture this kind of love.” </i><br/><br/>look, this was everything i wanted, and more. going into this novel, i wasn’t really expecting something that i would absolutely love. what i expected was a generic 3 star read that i’ll put off as <i>eh, contemporary isn’t really my preferred genre and that’s nothing new</i> but THIS is the kind of contemporary that i would die for time and time again.<br/><br/>everything leads to you is an</span>
  <span id="freeText8281590853452854107" style="display:none"><i> “as much as i had wanted a love story out of a movie, i know now that movies can only hope to capture this kind of love.” </i><br /><br />look, this was everything i wanted, and more. going into this novel, i wasn’t really expecting something that i would absolutely love. what i expected was a generic 3 star read that i’ll put off as <i>eh, contemporary isn’t really my preferred genre and that’s nothing new</i> but THIS is the kind of contemporary that i would die for time and time again.<br /><br />everything leads to you is an incredibly visual novel, which is due to nina lacour’s amazing writing. i’m not really a movie person but even so i could appreciate the descriptions of the sets and rooms and could literally picture every single thing.<br /><br />honestly, i did not care too much for the protagonist emi at first (and even forgot her name at one point in the beginning, but whatever i guess). as the story progressed, however, i grew more and more attached to her. ava, on the other hand, is a complete angel that i fell head over heels in love with from the start. she is the kind of person i would like to read more about in books. coming from an abusive household, she still manages to stay so incredibly strong and willing to change things about her life and the way she approaches situations. also, the mystery that surrounded her was really intriguing and kept me guessing if i’m not actually reading a mystery novel instead of a contemporary lmao.<br /><br />oh and of course, THE GAYNESS. very important. maybe the most important part of this. scratch everything i said up until now, it’s the gays that won be over. genuinely speaking, i could only name a single f/f book off the top of my head that i’ve read and if i think about it i could maybe come up with like five but that would be it. this story was just soo important, also for me personally, because emi was so open about her sexuality and that was really refreshing to read about. this whole story was so painfully beautiful and i’m so incredibly happy to have read and enjoyed it so much.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>→ 5 stars</i>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2456655735346588933"><b>4.5 stars. </b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>We love films because they make us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Emi Price is an aspiring production designer in Los Angeles, which means that she works behind the scenes on crafting film sets, searching for the perfect armchairs and potted plants and window dressings to make a scene feel real, unique, and personal. When s</span>
  <span id="freeText2456655735346588933" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars. </b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>We love films because they make us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Emi Price is an aspiring production designer in Los Angeles, which means that she works behind the scenes on crafting film sets, searching for the perfect armchairs and potted plants and window dressings to make a scene feel real, unique, and personal. When she and her best friend stumble across a mysterious letter hidden among a deceased actor’s possessions, though, they’re pulled into a real-life mystery as exciting as any film. <i>Everything Leads to You</i> is a sort of blend between mystery, coming-of-age story, and f/f romance, and it was such a sweet, fun read.<br /><br /><b>Elise described this as the “aesthetic lesbians” book, and I feel like that gives you a pretty good idea of what you’re in for here.</b> Reading this book feels like peeking through a rainbow kaleidoscope, like permanently seeing the world through that one snapchat filter that puts soft hearts over everything and glows with a really warm, ethereal light.<br /><br />This whole story is just soft and lovely and I was in my feelings a lot when I read this, okay?? There’s something about Nina LaCour’s writing that’s just…..so simple and soft and fresh and maybe this is a weird analogy but reading her books always feels like curling up in a pile of still-warm and freshly washed sheets.<br /><br /><b>In summary:</b> Very aesthetic. Much gay. 10/10 would recommend. <br /><br /><b>Diverse rep:</b> f/f, biracial MC<br /><b>CW:</b> mentions of homophobia &amp; drug use<br /><br />This review was also posted <a href="https://insearchofdragonsblog.wordpress.com/2018/04/16/four-mini-reviews-books-that-made-me-cry/" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog</a>.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755118446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17950518294275846563"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"Because in the conversation beneath this one, what we're really saying is I am an imperfect person. Here are my failures. Do you want me anyway?” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Awww, this was <b>so cute.</b> Seriously a nice palate cleanser in between all the angst and fantasy I’ve been reading lately. This story revolves around Emi, who whole working set design in LA stumbles onto a mystery involving a classic film star and a troubled girl named Ava. There's this really fantastic element of movie magic, and it was gre</span>
  <span id="freeText17950518294275846563" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Because in the conversation beneath this one, what we're really saying is I am an imperfect person. Here are my failures. Do you want me anyway?” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Awww, this was <b>so cute.</b> Seriously a nice palate cleanser in between all the angst and fantasy I’ve been reading lately. This story revolves around Emi, who whole working set design in LA stumbles onto a mystery involving a classic film star and a troubled girl named Ava. There's this really fantastic element of movie magic, and it was great reading about all the behind the scenes work.<br /><br />First off, <b>I am here for unapologetic lesbians.</b> Both Ava and Emi are open about liking girls, and neither was defined solely by their sexuality. The both had strong characters arcs, a cute romance and a role in the mystery. <br /><br />Emi's best friend Charlotte, was also great and a large example of the <b>strong theme of friendship</b> that took place. Charlotte and Emi were both devoted to each other, without enabling or pitying. <br /><br /><br />One problem I did have was with how much Emi idealized Morgan-- or I'm <b>told, but never shown</b> the idealization. Emi consistently thinks about how she shouldn't call Morgan, or how she wants to kiss Morgan, but that was it?? There was very little talk involving what it was about Morgan that Emi liked so much, and I still don't have any understanding of Morgan's personality.<br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> This was cute, lighthearted fun, and I'm ready ALWAYS ready for more F/F stories. But there was a lot of telling vs showing in the writing, and it felt like I was only seeing surface-level of most of the characters. <br /><br />Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27652389-emma?utm_medium=email&amp;utm_source=message" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma!</a></span>

<div id="review_897622364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/897622364" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/897622364?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=arc-galley-and-first-reads">arc-galley-and-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer897622364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4294337383828168388">Without a doubt, this is LaCour's best novel by far. While I've loved and taken away something different from every one of her books, I was still blown away by this which, believe me, is no easy task.<br/><br/><b>Film</b> <br/><br/>What I appreciate about LaCour's writing style, in general, is the fact that she never writes down to her audience. Instead of depicting young adults whose lives revolve around school, she imbibes each and every one of her protagonists which a passion. In <i>Hold Still</i> it was photography; in <i>The D</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4294337383828168388" style="display:none">Without a doubt, this is LaCour's best novel by far. While I've loved and taken away something different from every one of her books, I was still blown away by this which, believe me, is no easy task.<br /><br /><b>Film</b> <br /><br />What I appreciate about LaCour's writing style, in general, is the fact that she never writes down to her audience. Instead of depicting young adults whose lives revolve around school, she imbibes each and every one of her protagonists which a passion. In <i>Hold Still</i> it was photography; in <i>The Disenchantments</i> it was music; in <i>Everything Leads to You</i> it's film. Growing up in California with a family thoroughly invested in the film industry, Emi has almost always knows she wants a career in the movies. Not as an actress or a director or even a writer, but as a set designer. Through Emi's eyes, LaCour brings to life the thrill, the frustrations, and the importance of shaping a film set. Frankly speaking, I sort of want to fly to Hollywood myself, now, and decorate a few sets of my own. Emi's passion bleeds through the page and I <i>love</i> this. It makes her such a real, three-dimensional character. <br /><br />What's more, the film atmosphere of this entire story enables it to read much like a movie unfolding, scene-by-scene. <i>Everything Leads to You</i> isn't lacking in an action-filled and exciting plot line. Unlike LaCour's past novels, which have been primarily character-driven, introspective reads, her latest is a page-turning mystery (at first) which develops into a nail-biting romance. When Emi discovers a letter on set from a deceased, but legendary, actor she sets out, with the help of her best friend, to give it to its rightful owner. Emi tracks the recipient of this letter around town, eventually stumbling upon Ava, the grand-daughter of a famous Hollywood actor, and within moments, the course of her summer is changed. As Emi is offered a script to work on, she explores not only Ava's film talent--genetic--but also the secrets of Ava. With the backdrop of a film town, infused with characters thoroughly invested in movies, and with the additional inclusion of lines from Emi's new script, the setting of <i>Everything Leads to You</i> only adds to its story. LaCour has painted such a rich, vibrant atmosphere that it is impossible to look away; one must simply be content to be pulled into the tide. <br /><br /><b>Growth</b> <br /><br />LaCour's novels are all, in some way, shape, or form, about growth and <i>Everything Leads to You</i> is no exception. It's one of <i>those</i> books; you know, the novels where the protagonist discovers herself over the summer. It sounds incredibly cliched, but combined with LaCour's prose and command of characterization, it comes across as sophisticated and, most importantly, <i>real.</i> Emi, having just broken up with her on-again-off-again girlfriend yet <i>again</i> doesn't begin this novel in the best of places. Not only is she unable to leave her current relationship completely behind her, but she is also classically confident in her own capabilities in a manner only a teenager can possibly be. Over the course of the story, Emi grows to <i>mature,</i> if nothing else, admitting her faults and doing her best to rectify them. What's more, despite her sheltered and luxurious upbringing, at least compared to Ava's childhood which is riddled with far more economic struggles that Emi could imagine, Emi makes the effort to bridge that gap and understand not only Ava, but the world around her.<br /><br /><b>Romance</b> <br /><br />Lastly, I have to admit that the romance in this novel is simply to die-for. LaCour never emphasizes the fact that Emi and Ava like girls; it simply is. For once, I have to admit it's refreshing not to constantly re-hash the oppression homosexuals face and instead appreciate and enjoy a romance between two female characters. Even beyond that diverse aspect of the love story within these pages, though, LaCour goes above and beyond to create distinct, but powerful, secondary characters. Emi and Ava come from two completely different walks of life and are drawn together by their love for film, but the presence of these secondary characters helped to ground their romance to reality. With Emi and Ava, and their overblown enthusiasm for the scripts and sets in their lives, it is all too easy to fall into the fake, fleeting love story of Hollywood. Instead, LaCour uses her secondary characters as barriers between reality and fantasy, ensuring that Emi and Ava's path to one another is not half as easy as their first meeting. And, believe me, it's such a worthwhile romance. <br /><br /><i>Everything Leads to You</i> completely be-spelled me under its atmospheric setting, not to mention the glimpses it provided into the script Emi and Ava were working on during the summer. LaCour's small details, ultimately, elevate her novels from fiction to reality, breaking those barriers until her characters feel like living, breathing humans. It's a gift and with her latest, she uses that gift to her fullest capability. Yet another stunning novel from LaCour; I don't think anyone is surprised by that, least of all, me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4294337383828168388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1720357175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720357175" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720357175?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=f-f">f-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lesbian-mc">lesbian-mc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720357175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16520149788723578910"><i>
  <blockquote>“We love films because they make us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into the eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing. But also. They tell us to remember; they remind us of life. Remember, they say, how much it hurts to have your heartbroken.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>This is such a Classic in the lgbtq+ fiction scene, especially for wow & YA LGBT lit. I thought this was really sweet, and I actually liked </span>
  <span id="freeText16520149788723578910" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“We love films because they make us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into the eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing. But also. They tell us to remember; they remind us of life. Remember, they say, how much it hurts to have your heartbroken.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />This is such a Classic in the lgbtq+ fiction scene, especially for wow &amp; YA LGBT lit. I thought this was really sweet, and I actually liked it more than I thought I would. I guess I had it in my head it would be kind of stereotypical, but it actually had some really unique aspects. The main character, Emi, is a set designer, and I thought the descriptions of her job and how set design and what she's making acted as a metaphor for her emotions was nice. <br /><br />I also thought the representation was solid. It was nice to have a story about a lesbian who was secure in her identity. It was definitely not a coming out story and the romance actually takes more of a backseat then I thought in this book. But I thought Emi and Ava were sweet and I enjoyed them. <br /><br />I really liked the Hollywood mystery/unsolved aspects too. <br /><br />The reason for the lower rating is just that it didn't GRIP me. It didn't really capture my whole attention and I felt the characters could have had more depth. I do think it's a book I probably won't think about often now that I've finished it and I don't have a huge emotional attachment. That said, this is a 3.5 rating for me which is quite high for a YA contemporary romance. <br /><br />If you like books about Hollywood, Hollywood mysteries, lesbian main characters &amp; wlw fiction definitely you'd enjoy this<br /><br /><b>3.5 stars&gt;</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16520149788723578910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1550583018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1550583018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7729850087967252920">SO good. Perfect touch of mystery without actually being a mystery. I didn't want this to end!<br/><br/>F/f romance and the MC is 1/4 Black.<br/><br/><b>Audiobook review:</b> Narration was great! Would recommend. Some scenes seemed like they were script readings with stage directions, which might have had formatting in the print version, but I'm familiar with stage directions and didn't feel like anything was lost.<br/><br/>tw: death by overdose, toxic parent, teen homelessness.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1463989376" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463989376" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463989376?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142422946" href="/book/show/23281900-everything-leads-to-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2019">read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=all-the-pretty-covers">all-the-pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=books-owned-all-formats">books-owned-all-formats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=4stars">4stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=light-fiction">light-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463989376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14272442936602259028"><blockquote>
  <i>We love films because they make us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing. <br/>But also. <br/>They tell us to remember; they remind us of life. Remember, they say, how much it hurts to have your heart broken. Remember about death and suffering and the complexities of living. Remember what it is like to love someone. Remember how it is to be loved. Reme</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14272442936602259028" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>We love films because they make us feel something. They speak to our desires, which are never small. They allow us to escape and to dream and to gaze into eyes that are impossibly beautiful and huge. They fill us with longing. <br />But also. <br />They tell us to remember; they remind us of life. Remember, they say, how much it hurts to have your heart broken. Remember about death and suffering and the complexities of living. Remember what it is like to love someone. Remember how it is to be loved. Remember what you feel in this moment. Remember this. Remember this.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This was such a gorgeous book. It was absolutely beautifully written. I was completely enchanted by the Los Angeles setting and how it gave a glimpse into how movies are made. Nina LaCour just knows how to capture the essence of something and truly imparted so much atmosphere and emotion into this book. <br />I loved learning about Emi's life as a production designer in Hollywood. Her passion for films and film sets truly felt authentic and I was completely taken over by this intensity of hers. <br />Emi's friendship with Charlotte is just #goals. It's so nice to read a book where there is no toxicity between two female friends. They were both individual characters with their own unique thoughts and identities and their shared friendship just made them seem more rounded as people. Just hallelujah for women empowering other women. Even Emi's ex Morgan wasn't written as a heinous bitch type character as could have been so easy to do. God I just love reading about authentic female characters. <br />Also because this is Nina LaCour the book is properly diverse in a way that doesn't feel like it's pandering to some token gesture. And I just loved Emi's family, so nice to see a YA book with present parents that together with their children were just a great loving and supportive family. <br />But what was so great about the creation of Emi's character and her family storyline is that it provided the perfect counterpoint to Ava's storyline. Her family upbringing was far from ideal and I loved how the book showed her struggles as she came to learn more about where she came from. <br />And omg Emi and Ava together... Gaaaah I just ship them so hard. I loved how their love story was always hinted at under the surface but it gradually built up throughout the book... Slow burn heaven for sure!!! <br />This was such a cute read. It had all the magic of an old school motion picture mixed with sumptuous prose and relatable characters... A very happy <b>four stars</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <b>For more reviews and book related chat check out <a href="https://alittlehazebookblog.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a></b>
</i></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_935905060" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/935905060" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19112398-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460236247p2/19112398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/935905060?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/19112398-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who enjoy reading about first-world problems. </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sarah by: </span>
      Myself, because I'm a sucker for pretty covers and titles.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=oh-we-could-have-had-it-all">oh-we-could-have-had-it-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=we-need-diverse-books">we-need-diverse-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=no-thank-you">no-thank-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer935905060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8441360915578674074">My problem with <i>Everything leads to you</i> is how incredibly one-dimensional and shallow the story is.<br/>Everything is either modern! and chic! or vintage! and charming!, polished to perfection. There is very little realism. <br/>I always welcome diversity and was happy to see a a lesbian mixed race main character. <b>However</b>, you’re telling me she has never experienced discrimination, rejection or any type of struggle?<br/><b>I don’t buy it.</b><br/><br/>We’ve all been there. Someone said you can’t do it because of something irre</span>
  <span id="freeText8441360915578674074" style="display:none">My problem with <i>Everything leads to you</i> is how incredibly one-dimensional and shallow the story is.<br />Everything is either modern! and chic! or vintage! and charming!, polished to perfection. There is very little realism. <br />I always welcome diversity and was happy to see a a lesbian mixed race main character. <b>However</b>, you’re telling me she has never experienced discrimination, rejection or any type of struggle?<br /><b>I don’t buy it.</b><br /><br />We’ve all been there. Someone said you can’t do it because of something irrelevant. You can’t do it because you’re a girl, you can’t do it because it goes against the prejudices people have about you.<br />You can’t do it because you’re in a minority and different.<br />Apparently our MC is completely blind and inexperienced with all of this. <br /><br />Emi is privileged, extremely sheltered and knows nothing else than the glamorous side of Hollywod. <br />She’s given amazing opportunities at random, because she has contacts and never has to work hard for anything. <br />This girl is genuinely shocked when people don’t have the same condition and expectations as her, and that’s what made me loathe her.<br /><b>Ridiculously naive and wide-eyed, she jumps around like a goddamned fairy.</b><br />None of her flaws are pointed out, although I could find plenty. <br />The same goes for every single character, who who is confident, loved by everyone and have a cloud of creativity around them. <br /><br />Ask any 18-year-old what they want to do with their lives and get back a terrified look and realize they are lost.<br />Emi has everything figured out, zero real problems.<br />That’s why Ava’s story seems so forced; it’s pitiful but in a tragic sense you see in Hollywood movies without substance. It’s not real, and it pissed me off.<br /><br />These beautiful people are living their lives in beautiful Los Angeles (I’m not even hiding my jealousy), doing beautiful things.<br /><b>They should be on a kids’ show where everything is lovely and fun and BRIGHT.</b><br />Saying it’s shallow is an understatement,<br />Pair that with a slow, boring plot and you have a book I struggled to finish.<br /><br />I did enjoy how we found out a lot about the world of film-making and how Emi’s sexuality wasn’t the main point of the book. That’s it. <br />It’s fluffy and sweet but impersonal, fake and annoying.<br />2 generous stars, coming from someone who brought out their inner bitter emo baby for this review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8441360915578674074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_935525672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/935525672" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/935525672?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer935525672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10680040279307692300"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>With a mixture of Deb Caletti's quiet storytelling and Sarah Dessen's eye for detail, Nina LaCour writes the tale of Emi Price, an aspiring production designer who just graduated from high school. We first encounter Emi after her brother leaves her his polished Los Angeles apartment. His only instructions to her: do something amazing with the place. Emi feels at a loss until she and her best friend Charlotte stumble upon a mysterious letter at the old house of a deceased Hollywood legen</span>
  <span id="freeText10680040279307692300" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />With a mixture of Deb Caletti's quiet storytelling and Sarah Dessen's eye for detail, Nina LaCour writes the tale of Emi Price, an aspiring production designer who just graduated from high school. We first encounter Emi after her brother leaves her his polished Los Angeles apartment. His only instructions to her: do something amazing with the place. Emi feels at a loss until she and her best friend Charlotte stumble upon a mysterious letter at the old house of a deceased Hollywood legend. The message they find starts Emi on a journey to uncover the secrets of this old star's life, and along the way she may find some truths of her own.<br /><br />Nina LaCour has a subtle and effective writing style. She imbues Emi with a passion for production design, and from that LaCour crafts a simple, emotional story about film, love, and the intricacies of family. <i>Everything Leads to You</i> feels like one of those books that pertains to nothing and yet everything at once. LaCour slips in little passages of wisdom every now and then, and several aspects of this book stood out in a non-overbearing way: its sincere lesbian romance, its fleshed-out focus on Emi's design interests, and the misty nature of Ava's character.<br /><br />However, the book could have landed with more power in some parts. While LaCour has an elegant way of shaping her plot and developing Emi until her epiphanies, certain sections of the story lacked the emotional grip they would have had with a bit more emphasis or oomph. The themes of mysteries unraveling and accepting realities instead of false perceptions touched me. I just wish there could have been more substance to really make LaCour's main takeaways stellar (for example, by spending less time on Morgan, who contributed not too much to the story, while focusing more on the disparity of privilege between Emi and those around her).<br /><br />Overall, a good novel I would recommend to fans of <i>Hold Still</i> or fans of Deb Caletti and Sarah Dessen's more quiet stories. Nina LaCour has not blown me away with her writing yet, but I look forward to giving her next book another chance to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10680040279307692300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_941281033" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/941281033" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/941281033?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer941281033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer960609716698407481">This review appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/08/05/everything-leads-to-you-by-nina-lacour-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br/><br/>It’s not often I rate a contemporary 5 stars, but Everything Leads To You deserves every accolade. As a completely enchanting, elegant exploration of movie making in LA, it’s a story of hope, a young starlet and a designer, artistic passion and love that only grows when you give it a chance.<br/><br/>The novel starts off with a mystery, where Emi and her best friend Chantelle stumble upon a movie star’s inheritance letter, which leads</span>
  <span id="freeText960609716698407481" style="display:none">This review appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/08/05/everything-leads-to-you-by-nina-lacour-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br /><br />It’s not often I rate a contemporary 5 stars, but Everything Leads To You deserves every accolade. As a completely enchanting, elegant exploration of movie making in LA, it’s a story of hope, a young starlet and a designer, artistic passion and love that only grows when you give it a chance.<br /><br />The novel starts off with a mystery, where Emi and her best friend Chantelle stumble upon a movie star’s inheritance letter, which leads them to Ava, a budding starlet who just wants to know who her parents are. There’s a mystery and magic surrounding Ava, she’s a muse who is a blood relative to fame, and Emi just wants to know her.<br /><br />Unlike other LGBT books, Everything Leads to You is not purely about Emi’s sexuality. Liking other girls is something that she’s comfortable with and is a part of her. She doesn’t need to be shouting it from the rooftops or even broadcasting it to everyone she knows, she just lets it happen. This is how I think LGBT and diversity should be done – it’s just a part of the story, but not the ONLY part of the story.<br /><br />Emi’s romantic journey is tumultuous, as she learns to figure out what love she deserves. I loved how the romance was for all the right reasons, how Ava and Emi appreciated each other for who they were not who they wanted them to be or because it was convenient. It’s such a tentative journey, with both girls needing to work through their own lives but discovering parts of each other they loved.<br /><br />Emi’s role as an intern designer on a movie set was a fascinating part of the novel – it’s not often we learn about how movie sets are put together. Emi puts her heart and soul into her job, and her passion, talent and pride for her work shows. This dedication and focus was incredibly inspiring, especially when she had to struggle against real life career setbacks, such as limited budget, no pay and your boss not liking your ideas. But, the lessons she learns along the way and her pure dedication helps her spread her wings and succeed, which is something we can all learn from.<br /><br />I loved the wonderful, supportive friendship between Emi and Chantelle as well. No matter what, they had each other’s backs, whether it was to do with career, romance, the mystery or their friendship. These girls know each other’s strengths and weaknesses, and by standing together could they withstand any obstacle.<br /><br />Everything That Leads To You is one of my favourite LGBT contemporaries that I’ve ever read. I loved that magical, enchanting exploration into LA’s movie making industry, the mystery around Ava and the beautiful message of hope, passion and love by friends, family and others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="960609716698407481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_950316885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950316885" />
    <a title="Itsskelseyy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16519437-itsskelseyy"><img alt="Itsskelseyy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600973575p2/16519437.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950316885?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Itsskelseyy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Itsskelseyy" href="/user/show/16519437-itsskelseyy">Itsskelseyy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950316885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699820217243352584"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368123ra/720623.gif' width='200' height='100' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>So, this book, in lack of a better word, is awful.<br/><br/>There are so many problems with this book that I lost count while reading it so I'm going to try my best to be not spoilery and...nice.<br/><br/>I was told that every Nina LaCour book was good, but I don't think I'll be picking up another one anytime soon because her writing style is very similar to an amateur fan fiction writer. <br/><br/><i>"Oh," Ava says, looking at the screen. "The internet is locked or something."<br/>"You just need a password. The front desk will giv</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3699820217243352584" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368123ra/720623.gif" width="200" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So, this book, in lack of a better word, is awful.<br><br>There are so many problems with this book that I lost count while reading it so I'm going to try my best to be not spoilery and...nice.<br><br>I was told that every Nina LaCour book was good, but I don't think I'll be picking up another one anytime soon because her writing style is very similar to an amateur fan fiction writer. <br><br><i>"Oh," Ava says, looking at the screen. "The internet is locked or something."<br>"You just need a password. The front desk will give it to us."<br>Ava stands up and grabs the key.<br>"You can call them."<br>I cross to the desk, pick up the phone and dial zero.<br>"Hey," I say. "What's the internet password?"<br>I read it out to Ava and she enters it. She smiles.<br>"Success," I tell the man on the other end. "Thanks."</i><br><br>^Yes that is actually in the book. And yes you literally could sum that entire situation up in one sentence to: "Recognizing that the internet was not connected, I called the front desk for the wifi password." And that's not even a good sentence! <br><br>The amount of unneeded dialogue was way too extreme. It wasn't even portrayed interesting at all. I felt like I was reading a text conversation between two 13 year olds half the time. A lot of the dialogue was things that no reader would even care about, such as giving EXACT directions to a shopping store ( I'm talking road names and when to turn, etc). The imagery she decided to add to the book didn't even add to the setting at all. The main character is supposed to be a production designer and the author can't even design her own settings.<br><br>Speaking of characters I like how Emi isn't given any physical characteristics at all and about halfway into the book you find out she's partially black. I was picturing some spunky blonde this entire time because she is never once given any physical characteristic throughout the book. But when Ava enters the room her entire physical appearance is described the same way that all the other character's physical appearance is described: How their hair is styled and what they're wearing. There is no background whatsoever of how Emi and Charlotte became friends (none that I remember) and also no background on how they obtained the internships onto a famous movie set. I also like how Emi's brother gives them his apartment for two months and THAT night they literally move in without consulting their parents or talking it over at all. This book did a great job of giving a lot of unneeded information but lacking the actual information the reader wants. <br><br>I'm also going to briefly touch on the gay pairing. Don't worry, you find out Emi is immediately gay as soon as you open the first page. Since the LGBT community is taken very well amongst society today (including myself) I feel like Nina La Cour was trying WAY too hard to make this "normal" so to speak. There is a very tasteful way to present a gay couple normally in a book without the reader giving a second thought but La Cour just did not make it happen. She's gay La Cour, I get it. <br><br>Can I also talk about how predictable this book is?! It's supposed to be about this mystery letter that Emi and Charlotte find and how they want to discover its secrets and all this other bull crap. The mystery is solved in 50 pages, very easily by the way, who they encounter a girl their age (WHAT NO?!) and Emi confesses that all of their evidence "Led to her." (Really....really...?) Side note, I hate books that use the title of their book 75 pages in. It gives away WAY too much to the reader, aka the entire rest of the book.<br><br>Why did I keep reading? I read a review here that said it picks up about 150 pages in. It didn't. But I was determined to finish it. Turned out to be a huge waste of time. The worst book I've read this year.There wasn't a single theme in this book that I could name that even mattered. This book literally could have been 90 pages long. It would be considered a middle grade book if it wasn't about a lesibian couple and didn't throw the F bomb out once in awhile. So now, I'm finishing my very first lengthly review I've ever written because I don't want anyone else to go through the torture that this book held for me.<br><br>1 star for poor effort.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3699820217243352584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer573306588557409032">Well.... Technically I would give this a 2 star rating but the Hollywood setting was just amazing I had to give it another star.<br/><br/>I'm a huge, HUGE movie buff. And not the type that just binge-watch films... I look at everything; the direction, acting, lighting, sets, cinematography, the details. So this book really hit home for me. The fact that the protagonist is a budding set designer just fascinated me. I loved the way the book describes the world she's in and her job so vividly.<br/><br/>However, that i</span>
  <span id="freeText573306588557409032" style="display:none">Well.... Technically I would give this a 2 star rating but the Hollywood setting was just amazing I had to give it another star.<br /><br />I'm a huge, HUGE movie buff. And not the type that just binge-watch films... I look at everything; the direction, acting, lighting, sets, cinematography, the details. So this book really hit home for me. The fact that the protagonist is a budding set designer just fascinated me. I loved the way the book describes the world she's in and her job so vividly.<br /><br />However, that is the only thing I liked about this book. Some parts were just unrealistic for me--- Ava's development was just too Cinderella-ish, I can't help but roll my eyes. Most of this book was just too unbelievable. <br /><br />I did appreciate the LGBTQ+ aspects of this book though. It wasn't a sob story or any coming out struggle. The characters knew they were gay from the get go. So I really liked that. <br /><br />But unfortunately I couldn't really love this book. I didn't expect much, but I was still disappointed.</span>

<div id="review_2293173831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2293173831" />
    <a title="Enne (they/he)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60021454-enne-they-he"><img alt="Enne (they/he)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577868041p2/60021454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2293173831?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Enne (they/he)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Enne (they/he)" href="/user/show/60021454-enne-they-he">Enne (they/he)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=z-2018-reads">z-2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=rep-lgbtqiap-main">rep-lgbtqiap-main</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=dissapointed">dissapointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=rep-lgbtqiap">rep-lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2293173831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8611909462927018562"><blockquote>
  <i>”There are no scenes in life, there are only minutes. And none are skipped over and they all lead to the next.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><b>2 stars </b><br/><b>TW:</b>n/a<br/><i>read full review <a href='bookishbooknerd.wordpress.com/2018/03/31/everything-leads-to-you-book-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a><br/>*full review include favorite quotes and a spoiler section</i><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Writing</u>
</b><br/>Okay, so, the writing wasn’t bad. It just wasn’t for me, personally. I found myself trudging through it because it felt so bland and was not expressive of Emi’s character at all, in my opinion. Like, there was absolutely nothing done for me to distinguish Emi’s character from </span>
  <span id="freeText8611909462927018562" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>”There are no scenes in life, there are only minutes. And none are skipped over and they all lead to the next.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><b>2 stars </b><br /><b>TW:</b>n/a<br /><i>read full review <a href="bookishbooknerd.wordpress.com/2018/03/31/everything-leads-to-you-book-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br />*full review include favorite quotes and a spoiler section</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Writing</u>
</b><br />Okay, so, the writing wasn’t bad. It just wasn’t for me, personally. I found myself trudging through it because it felt so bland and was not expressive of Emi’s character at all, in my opinion. Like, there was absolutely nothing done for me to distinguish Emi’s character from any other YA heroine and I found that to be kind of disappointing. Just my opinion, though.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Plot/Pacing</u>
</b><br />Okay, so this is my main problem with this book. It was just so slow. Especially the romance aspect of it – but I was okay with that. The thing that bothered me the most was that the plot couldn’t seem to find one thing to focus on. And I understand the importance of subplots, trust me, I do, but the thing that bothered me was that the book couldn’t seem to decide which plot was the main one and which one was the subplot, which led to a jumbled mess of a book where nothing really moves forward until the last 75-100 pages.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br />Oh, look, another problem I had with this is that none of the characters have a multi-dimensional personality, save for maybe Emi, but that’s debatable too. They are all so one-sided and that made them not interesting to read about at all. I just wanted to relate to them, but I couldn’t because all they ever talked about is either their movie business stuff or Ava’s grandfather. And don’t get me wrong, I loved the sneak peek we got into the movie business, I just wish that wasn’t all the characters talked about.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Overall</u>
</b><br />I think others would enjoy this book more than I did, but this just wasn’t for me. I do love some of the themes explored in it, though, definitely, and I love the fact that this is a story about a gay girl and it isn’t entirely focused on the coming out process, which is definitely something we need more of in YA. But that’s all.<br /><br />~~~<br />gay fluff? <br />gay fluff.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
