        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2130850282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9264591126006507448">[3.5]<br/>Nina Lacour has a way with words. Incredible way with words! I'm not a movie buff, but this book made me want to become one. And r made me appreciate the art that goes into creating visual stories. <br/>Emi was a great main character! The passion she had for her job really came through and I loved the way she saw the world. She's a romantic at heart about everything. <br/>I feel like we just scratched the surface with the characters though. I desperately wanted more development. The romance also deve</span>
  <span id="freeText9264591126006507448" style="display:none">[3.5]<br />Nina Lacour has a way with words. Incredible way with words! I'm not a movie buff, but this book made me want to become one. And r made me appreciate the art that goes into creating visual stories. <br />Emi was a great main character! The passion she had for her job really came through and I loved the way she saw the world. She's a romantic at heart about everything. <br />I feel like we just scratched the surface with the characters though. I desperately wanted more development. The romance also developed too quickly for my liking.. Or it didn't feel convincing enough, because of the lack of growth or substance in the relationship. <br /><br />Other than that, I highly enjoyed it. The book really came to life when the movie aspects were depicted and it was beautiful to read. I can't wait to see what more Nina Lacour writes. I know I'll read it all! </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/905844306?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/12842423-jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer905844306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer879446745985806005">*I received this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review*<br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. This was my first book by Nina LaCour and I loved her style and the tone overall. The <i>only problem</i> I had was I felt like it was just a touch <i>slow</i> in the middle, but it picked up and I really enjoyed it!<br/><br/>I loved the plot surrounding film-making and of course the mystery they encountered. I really enjoyed all of the characters in this book, especially the mysterious Ava. These characters w</span>
  <span id="freeText879446745985806005" style="display:none">*I received this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review*<br /><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. This was my first book by Nina LaCour and I loved her style and the tone overall. The <i>only problem</i> I had was I felt like it was just a touch <i>slow</i> in the middle, but it picked up and I really enjoyed it!<br /><br />I loved the plot surrounding film-making and of course the mystery they encountered. I really enjoyed all of the characters in this book, especially the mysterious Ava. These characters were flawed, yet seemed so real to me and I love reading about characters like that. <br /><br />I appreciated that the main character was open about her sexual orientation and instead of this being a coming out story, Nina LaCour just made it a part of <i>who</i> Emi was. I've read stories where the secondary characters were gay, but not the main character so this was a first for me. I loved that our main character wasn't struggling with how she felt, but accepted it. I'll admit I was frustrated with Emi in the beginning because of her poor relationship choices (just learn how to walk away girl! she doesn't love you!) but I grew to love her. <br /><br />Honestly, while reading this book, it almost felt like I was becoming friends with Ava, Charlotte, Emi, and Jamal. You see them for who they are, their flaws included, but despite it all you grow to love them all the same. I finished this book feeling happy and it gave me closure (which we all know I love.)<br /><br />I like that this book encourages you to not wait, but to <u>act</u>. You never know how much time you'll have.</span>
  <a data-text-id="879446745985806005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2111200898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10013077070419313514">Yes, I am giving Nina LaCour yet another (well deserved) 5 star rating. <br/><br/>I've read 3 of her books this past week and I can't get enough, they are all beautiful, and so, so heartbreaking. <br/><br/>This review will probably be an emotional mess because I am literally <i>still</i> crying, but I'll try my best. I picked this book up expecting a sweet F/F romance, with a bit of mystery and lots of movie magic, but I got so much more. I should know by now that LaCour takes every expectation and flips it on it's head. </span>
  <span id="freeText10013077070419313514" style="display:none">Yes, I am giving Nina LaCour yet another (well deserved) 5 star rating. <br /><br />I've read 3 of her books this past week and I can't get enough, they are all beautiful, and so, so heartbreaking. <br /><br />This review will probably be an emotional mess because I am literally <i>still</i> crying, but I'll try my best. I picked this book up expecting a sweet F/F romance, with a bit of mystery and lots of movie magic, but I got so much more. I should know by now that LaCour takes every expectation and flips it on it's head. This was not a book about love. This was a book about loss, and pain, and finding yourself.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I like slow burn romance, but holy sh*t. This was more like, "when is she going to light the candle?" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I wish I had read the last half at home so I could've cried my eyes out properly, I was really close to shedding a tear in the middle of my class. Oh, you don't read when you're supposed to be paying attention? Yeah.... me neither. <br /><br />LaCour draws readers in with easy going, lovable characters and intricate story lines, but once she has you she will not let go until she has shattered your heart into a million pieces. The deeper you go into her novels, the more flawed and realistic the characters become. She will never be the kind of writer who has flat characters, or instant romances. The relationships and lives of the characters are messy because <i>real life</i> is messy.</span>

<div id="review_2211160081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2211160081" />
    <a title="Chelsea slytherink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33481873-chelsea-slytherink"><img alt="Chelsea slytherink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550223913p2/33481873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2211160081?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea slytherink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea slytherink" href="/user/show/33481873-chelsea-slytherink">Chelsea slytherink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142422946" href="/book/show/23281900-everything-leads-to-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=representation-queer">representation-queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2211160081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16519845904322392902"><b>Check out <a href='http://romweasley.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog</a> for more reviews and other bookish posts! This is a spoiler-free review!</b><br/><br/>Everything Leads To You has received many positive reviews and We Are Okay by Nina LaCour is one of my favourite books of 2017, so I had expected to love this novel as well. Unfortunately, I didn’t. This is by no means a bad book, I just had expected something more profound.<br/><br/>My main problem is that this is a young adult contemporary, yet it is neither realistic or relatable. Emi is an eighteen-year-old set d</span>
  <span id="freeText16519845904322392902" style="display:none"><b>Check out <a href="http://romweasley.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> for more reviews and other bookish posts! This is a spoiler-free review!</b><br /><br />Everything Leads To You has received many positive reviews and We Are Okay by Nina LaCour is one of my favourite books of 2017, so I had expected to love this novel as well. Unfortunately, I didn’t. This is by no means a bad book, I just had expected something more profound.<br /><br />My main problem is that this is a young adult contemporary, yet it is neither realistic or relatable. Emi is an eighteen-year-old set designer who at the start of the book is still in high school as well. Though it was nice to learn more about the film industry, I couldn’t relate to the characters and their experiences because it seemed so far-fetched. They have jobs on film-sets while attending a private high school, have enough spare time to go wherever they want AND their parents are never around? Their lives seemed so perfect, it just didn’t seem real.<br /><br />It took me five days to finish this book, even though it’s only 300 pages long and I picked it up regularly! The pacing was odd: a lot of time was spent learning more about Ava’s family, but I didn’t care to learn more about her. It wasn’t as if there was much of a mystery to solve.<br /><br />Though you can’t tell while looking at the cover, the protagonist of this book is biracial. Her grandfather was black, so she refers to herself as “I’m a quarter”. I feel the need to include this in my review because I know some multiracial people aren’t fond of expressions like that.<br /><br />There were some things that bothered me, but they weren’t a huge deal in the book. Firstly, Emi says “I wore a skimpy shirt to show off my girlishness”. This rubbed me the wrong way because it sounds as if you can’t be girly if you for example don’t have breasts to show off.<br /><br />I also didn’t like how Laura was presented. It seemed as if she only wanted to be queer in order to gain popularity, in order to be liked by the boys. Yes, many allocishet boys and men are aroused by femme queer girls, but that’s not at all a compliment. It’s objectifying and fetishising. There would still be a lot of anti-queerness coming from other people, so this doesn’t add up.<br /><br />There was only one closeted queer girl in this book and I felt like she was presented as some sort of “villain”, because she claimed the other girl had tricked her. The closeted girl’s family was very religious, which is why she was afraid to come out. I understand this hurt her girlfriend, but this narrative hurts, especially because there weren’t any other closeted queer characters who were presented in a more positive light.<br /><br />Even though this review is rather negative, I ended up giving this book 3.5 stars. Like I said, it’s not a bad book, I just didn’t love it.<br /><br />content and trigger warnings for: a lot of ableist language (such as crazy and insane), breaking and entering, homeless shelter, deceased parents, adoption, anti-queerness, overdose, drug use, underage drinking<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16519845904322392902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1698306317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698306317" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1698306317?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698306317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17820917611207151621"><em>Everything Leads to You</em> was the last of my <a href='http://prettybooks.co.uk/2017/06/04/summer-has-begun/' rel='nofollow noopener'>summer reads</a> and I chose it over <em>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28243032.We_Are_Okay' title='We Are Okay by Nina LaCour' rel='nofollow noopener'>We Are Okay</a>
</em>, a story that sounds a lot sadder and darker – I'll save it for autumn!<br/><br/>I finished <em>Everything Leads to You</em> a couple of weeks ago and I still remember how film aspect of the storyline made me feel. I <em>adored</em> it. I love the idea of being a set designer like Emi, our talented protagonist, and Nina LaCour tackles every little detail. She enables the reader to really understand and picture the work that goes int</span>
  <span id="freeText17820917611207151621" style="display:none"><em>Everything Leads to You</em> was the last of my <a href="http://prettybooks.co.uk/2017/06/04/summer-has-begun/" rel="nofollow noopener">summer reads</a> and I chose it over <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28243032.We_Are_Okay" title="We Are Okay by Nina LaCour" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are Okay</a>
</em>, a story that sounds a lot sadder and darker – I'll save it for autumn!<br /><br />I finished <em>Everything Leads to You</em> a couple of weeks ago and I still remember how film aspect of the storyline made me feel. I <em>adored</em> it. I love the idea of being a set designer like Emi, our talented protagonist, and Nina LaCour tackles every little detail. She enables the reader to really understand and picture the work that goes into set design, why it's such an important part of making a film, and how <em>fun</em> it can be. Emi is incredibly passionate about her future career, but Nina doesn't just show us the glamorous side. We also see the boring, frustrating side of the industry, from being a lowly intern and not feeling good enough to browsing hundreds of sofas to find <em>the one</em>.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Continue reading this review over on <a href="https://prettybooks.co.uk/2017/08/28/what-ive-read-everything-leads-to-you-the-loneliest-girl-in-the-universe-editing-emma/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17820917611207151621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QL9zQEvyt4Dyp4OodVb1BW/1sXYeZGQqMRtjbsKb//EF4vTf61fCaxSDutciSthyzyY5jAZ+W7K91pKpms4xvg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z02lNtrHY/5Xe4dIbDtj06+3pwTizaduBEl61vhM6mqKECKpemIWFbFfvjc7J06kD2Qv/vrXmPaIhIsRoBkkJQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour">About Nina LaCour</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1282077633p3/2889003.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour">Nina LaCour

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17303035008742535122">Nina LaCour grew up in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her first job was at fourteen in an independent bookstore, and she has since worked in two others. She has tutored and taught in various places, from a juvenile hall to a private college. She now teaches English at an independent high school.<br/><br/>Of Hold Still, Nina says:<br/><br/>“This book is about loss, and it’s also about art. The loss part comes from a clas</span>
  <span id="freeText17303035008742535122" style="display:none">Nina LaCour grew up in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her first job was at fourteen in an independent bookstore, and she has since worked in two others. She has tutored and taught in various places, from a juvenile hall to a private college. She now teaches English at an independent high school.<br /><br />Of Hold Still, Nina says:<br /><br />“This book is about loss, and it’s also about art. The loss part comes from a classmate’s suicide. I didn’t know him well, but learning of his death remains one of the most profoundly sad and confusing events of my teenage years. The art part comes from my mother, a high school photography teacher. A girl in one of her student’s photographs inspired the character of Ingrid. While I was writing, I learned how to develop and print black-and-white photographs in a darkroom.”<br /><br />Nina lives in Oakland, California with her wife and their two cute cats. Visit her online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ninalacour.com">www.ninalacour.com</a>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17303035008742535122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
